Build something new, such as a complete, working app from a standing start. Or bring your product and point Claude at the biggest problem it's facing. ### 🤖 Assistant

Locked in:
- **Cloud VM, everything on it** → real public URLs for the control plane *and* every managed deployment (via reverse proxy). I'll build locally and deploy to the VM mid-afternoon.
- **I'm the whole build team** → I own all files and will fan out parallel agents against a shared skeleton with clean contracts.
- **In-app git-backed VCS + PR view** → bulletproof, on-brand, no GitHub dependency.

One dependency to line up now (don't let it block us): for the "Cloud VM, everything on it" path I'll need **SSH access to a Linux VM** (or cloud creds to provision one). ### projects/services.py
- `detect_runtime(path)` — Django via manage.py at root or one level down (sets `app_subdir`, picks `requirements.txt` near manage.py or repo root else `pip install django`, `runserver 0.0.0.0:$PORT`); Procfile `web:` line; generic fallback.
- `import_project(name, repo_url, description="")` — slugifies (idempotent collision → `-2`, `-3`), clones into `HELM_REPOS_DIR/&lt;slug&gt;` (https / file:// / bare path all via `git clone &lt;url&gt; &lt;dest&gt;`), resolves default branch (`symbolic-ref` then `rev-parse --abbrev-ref`), runs detect_runtime, creates staging+prod Environments on the default branch, sets status READY (FAILED + import_log on error), logs Events (rocket/check/x).

### deploys/services.py
- `allocate_port` (skips LIVE-deployment ports + OS-bound), `deploy`, `stop` (os.killpg group, SIGTERM→SIGKILL), `restart`, `health_ch
… [truncated 3295 chars] …

It also surfaced a subtle **SQLite bug**: `F("output") + chunk` does *numeric* coercion on SQLite (turns text into `0`), so it used `Concat(F(...), Value(...))` instead — and flagged that the model's `append_output()` has the same latent bug for me to fix at integration. Sharp catch.

### 🤖 Assistant

The demo imported + deployed both environments LIVE. But I've spotted an architecture risk: the log-ingestion tee thread lives in whatever process calls `deploy()`, and the app's stdout is a **pipe** owned by that process. When `helm_demo` exits, ingestion stops and the orphaned app can crash on its next log write (EPIPE). For a live demo that's fragile.

The robust fix: write app output to a **file** (so apps survive any parent) and have the server **tail the file** to ingest. Let me look at the current spawn and refactor:

**🔧 Read**

```
/Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon/deploys/services.py
```

### 🤖 Assistant

**🔧 Bash**

```
cd /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon
# kill orphaned pocketshop apps from the earlier (pipe-based) run
for p in 9101 9102 9103 9104; do
  pid=$(lsof -nP -iTCP:$p -sTCP:LISTEN -t 2>/dev/null)
  [ -n "$pid" ] && kill -9 $pid 2>/dev/null && echo "killed $pid on $p"
done
echo "=== pocketshop checkout + promo logic ==="
sed -n '1,200p' sample_apps/pocketshop/store/promos.py 2>/dev/null
echo "=========== views (checkout/cart) ==========="
grep -n "def \|promo\|cart\|session\|BOGO" sample_apps/pocketshop/store/views.py | head -40
```

<details><summary>tool result</summary>

```
killed 96624 on 9101
killed 96872 on 9102
=== pocketshop checkout + promo logic ===
"""Promo code logic for checkout.

PocketShop supports a few promo codes. Most are simple percentage / flat
discounts. The BOGO ("buy one, get one") code is more involved: it finds the
qualifying items in the cart and gives the cheapest qualifying unit for free,
spread across the qualifying lines.

NOTE FOR MAINTAINERS: the BOGO branch has a long-standing latent bug — see
README.md ("The planted bug"). It only manifests when BOGO is applied to a
cart that contains no qualifying ("pair"/"set") items, which is why it slipped
past normal testing.
"""
from decimal import Decimal


class PromoError(Exception):
    """Raised for a user-facing, recoverable promo problem (e.g. unknown code)."""


def normalize(code):
    return (code or "").strip().upper()


def apply_promo(code, lines, subtotal):
    """Return the discount Decimal for ``code`` applied to ``lines``.

    ``lines`` is a list of CartLine-like objects (``.product``, ``.quantity``,
    ``.line_total``). ``subtotal`` is the cart subtotal as a Decimal.

    Raises PromoError for an unknown code. Returns Decimal("0") for no code.
    """
    code

def add_to_cart(request, slug):
    product = get_object_or_404(Product, slug=slug)
    cart = Cart(request)
    cart.add(product)
    messages.success(request, f"Added {product.name} to your cart.")
    return redirect("store:cart")


def cart_view(request):
    cart = Cart(request)
    if request.method == "POST":
        # Quantity updates from the cart page.
        for line in cart.lines():
            field = f"qty_{line.product.id}"
            if field in request.POST:
                try:
                    cart.set_quantity(line.product.id, int(request.POST[field]))
                except (TypeError, ValueError):
                    pass
        remove_id = request.POST.get("remove")
        if remove_id:
            cart.remove(remove_id)

### 🤖 Assistant

Found a real proxy bug: `requests` collapses multiple `Set-Cookie` headers into one comma-joined string, so session cookies break through the proxy — which is why the cart stays empty. The storefront's cart (and the demo) depends on cookies. Let me fix the proxy to forward each `Set-Cookie` individually:

**🔧 Read**

```
/Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon/deploys/views.py
```

<details><summary>tool result</summary>

107	    response = HttpResponse(
108	        content,
109	        status=upstream_resp.status_code,
110	        content_type=upstream_resp.headers.get("Content-Type"),
111	    )
112	    for key, value in upstream_resp.headers.items():
113	        if key.lower() in _HOP_BY_HOP or key.lower() == "content-type":
114	            continue
115	        response[key] = value
116	    return response

from django.db import models


class Product(models.Model):
    """A single sellable item in the PocketShop catalog."""

    class Meta:

### 🤖 Assistant

🎯 **Detection works end-to-end:** BOGO with a non-qualifying item → 500 → app logs to file → server tailer ingests → traceback assembled → **INC-1 created** (ValueError, `store/promos.py:61`, "min() arg is an empty sequence", full traceback captured). The suspect file is correctly relative for the agent's worktree.

Now the money shot — the autonomous fix. First a quick sanity check that `claude` headless works with our exact invocation/model before spending a full agent run:

**🔧 Bash**

```
cd /tmp && rm -rf claude_sanity && mkdir claude_sanity && cd claude_sanity
git init -q && git config user.email t@t.co && git config user.name t
echo "start" > seed.txt && git add -A && git commit -qm init
echo "=== claude headless sanity (model claude-opus-4-8) ==="
claude -p "Create a file called hello.txt containing exactly the word: hi" \
  --output-format stream-json --verbose --permission-mode acceptEdits \
  --dangerously-skip-permissions --model claude-opus-4-8 2>&1 | tail -8
echo "=== result ==="
ls -la hello.txt 2>&1 && cat hello.txt 2>&1
```

**🔧 Bash**

cd /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon
if [ -f ~/dev/palimpsest/.env.local ]; then
  key=$(grep -iE "ANTHROPIC_API_KEY" ~/dev/palimpsest/.env.local | head -1 | sed -E 's/.*=//; s/^["'\'' ]+//; s/["'\'' ]+$//')
  if [ -n "$key" ]; then
    # store locally for our own agents + later VM deploy; do NOT print the secret
    printf 'ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=%s\n' "$key" > .env.helm.local
    chmod 600 .env.helm.local
    echo "API key found: yes | length ${#key} | prefix ${key:0:8}… | saved to .env.helm.local (gitignored)"
  else
    echo "ANTHROPIC_API_KEY not found in file"
    grep -oiE "^[A-Z_]+=" ~/dev/palimpsest/.env.local | head
  fi
else
  echo "file not found"
fi
# ensure the local secret file is gitignored
grep -q ".env.helm.local" .gitignore || printf ".env.helm.local\n" >> .gitignore
echo "gitignore ok"
```

## What we built: **Hull** — the autonomous software operating system

One Django control plane, operated by Claude Opus 4.8 agents, that unifies what normally takes GitHub + Vercel + PagerDuty + Datadog — and runs it autonomously. **Live at https://54.185.134.217.sslip.io**

### The two flows, both working end-to-end
1. **Autonomous incident→fix (the money shot):** a prod error is captured from live logs → PagerDuty-style **incident** opens → a Claude agent spins an isolated **git worktree** → fixes the root cause + **adds a regression test** → opens a **PR** → **CI** runs the suite → green → **merges** → **redeploys** → incident **RESOLVED**. No human.
2. **Feature flow:** spin a worktree → agent builds a feature → PR + diff → CI → merge → deploy (verified live with a "free shipping" banner).

Plus: repo **import** + runtime detection, **staging/prod deployments** as managed processes behind a reverse proxy with public URLs, in-app **git-backed PR/diff/merge** UI, **logs/metrics/incidents** observability, and **Temporal** orchestration (with a threaded fallback).

## How we built it (the orchestration story for the judges)
- I wrote a **foundation** first: data model + per-app **service contracts** + UI design system, all in `CONTRACTS.md`.
- Then **4 Claude agents built disjoint slices in parallel** against those frozen contracts (projects/deploys · agents/vcs · observability/orchestration · the PocketShop sample app).
- "Done" is **model-verifiable**: `rubric.md` (100 pts, every item a pass/fail HTTP/DB assertion), a green test suite, and a **one-command** reproducible demo: `helm_demo --break`.
- Captured in `workflows/build_helm.workflow.js`. The naming itself used a **generate-and-filter workflow** (39 candidates → 28 web-vetted → ranked → you picked **Hull**).

## Self-caught failures (judges love these)
- An agent's deploys failed because managed apps inherited Hull's `DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE` → it diagnosed and added `_clean_env()`.
- Integration caught the same class of bug in CI, plus a **proxy `Set-Cookie` bug** (broke sessions/cart) and a **SQLite `F()+text` coercion bug**.

## Verified
- ✅ Local: both flows end-to-end, 9 unit tests green, all routes 200
- ✅ Cloud: provisioned EC2 in `reserv-dev`/us-west-2 myself (t3.xlarge, Caddy TLS, Claude CLI + your API key), public URL serving Hull
- 🔄 Cloud autonomous loop: **running now** (agent mid-fix)

## Infra I created (tagged `Project=hull-hackathon`, teardown ready)
- EC2 `i-0f489356fa403c55b` @ 54.185.134.217, SG `hull-demo-sg`, key pair `hull-demo` (PEM gitignored). One-command cleanup: `deploy/teardown.sh`.

### 🤖 Assistant

This is the fun part. Love the ambition — and you're right, we have all day. Let me lock the vision, propose the agent org + workflow harness, and confirm a few architectural forks before I spin it up.

## Vision — here's what I'm hearing (the product roadmap)

Hull becomes a genuinely enterprise-grade, multi-tenant autonomous engineering platform:

| Section | Target bar | Status |
|---|---|---|
| **Accounts & Tenancy** | Orgs, users, roles/RBAC, invites, login/SSO-ready — everything org-scoped | 🆕 foundational |
| **Deploys & Environments** | Complex apps: web + **Postgres + async workers + Redis**, per-env config/secrets | ⬆️ rearchitect |
| **Domains** | **Custom domain per project/env** (hostname, not path), configurable | ⬆️ rearchitect |
| **Observability** | **Datadog-level**: structured logs + search, metrics (p50/p95/p99, error rate, throughput), dashboards, alerts | ⬆️ major upgrade |
| **Incidents** | **PagerDuty-level**: severities, on-call, escalation, timelines, postmortems, ack/resolve | ⬆️ major upgrade |
| **Issues (Jira)** | Boards, tickets, sprints, assignees, labels, links to PRs/incidents — *the agent backlog lives here* | 🆕 |
| **Docs / Wiki** | Spaces, pages, hierarchy, search, knowledge vault, linked to code | 🆕 |
| **Agents & Orchestration** | The agent org surfaced in-product | ⬆️ |

Crown jewel — the **autonomous incident→fix loop** — stays sacred; we evolve *around* it, never break it.

## The agent org ("Gastown") — the workflow harness I'll build

- **Mayor = this thread (me + you).** Live direction, feedback, sprint kickoffs. You and I steer; teams build autonomously in the background.
- **Chief PM agent** — ideates the overall vision/roadmap *with your input via me*, prioritizes each sprint, writes acceptance rubrics. (`docs/ROADMAP.md`)
- **Section PM agents** (one per section) — own a PRD + rubric + ticket backlog (`docs/prd/<section>.md`). Strategy: **generate-and-filter** (propose features → filter to sprint MVP).
- **Builder agents** — implement tickets in **isolated git worktrees** (so parallel work never collides).
- **Adversarial QA agents** — verify against each section's rubric, *try to break it*, file bugs. Strategy: **adversarial verification + loop-until-done** (re-dispatch builders until the rubric passes or N rounds).
- **Integrator/Synthesizer** — merge worktrees, run migrations + full test suite, boot-check, redeploy to the live VM. Strategy: **fan-out & synthesize**.

Each `Workflow` invocation = **one sprint**; between sprints I report to you and take new direction.

## Architectural implications I'd bake in
- **Evolve in place** on the current stack; **migrate control-plane DB SQLite → Postgres** (multitenancy + concurrency; also kills the flaky-test issue).
- **Multitenancy is cross-cutting** (every model gets an `Org` FK) → it must land in a **foundation sprint first**, before feature fan-out, or we get massive rework.

Four forks I want your call on before I build the harness:

### 🤖 Assistant

🏗️ **The Gastown build org is live — Sprint 0 (Foundation) is running autonomously.** You can watch it with `/workflows`.

## What's executing right now
The harness is running the org against `docs/ROADMAP.md`:
- **PLAN** — two section PM agents (Accounts & Tenancy, Docker-Deploys & Domains) are writing `docs/prd/<section>.md` with requirements + machine-checkable rubrics + ticket lists (generate-and-filter).
- **BUILD** — then builders implement. Tenancy runs **first** (it's cross-cutting: adds an `Org` FK to every model + auth + scoping); deploys-v2 follows.
- **QA** — an adversarial reviewer checks each build against its rubric and **loops the builder until it's green** (2 rounds).
- **SYNTHESIZE** — an integrator wires shared files, migrates, runs tests, boots, and **regression-gates the autonomous incident→fix loop**.

## How we work now (the model you wanted)
- **You + I are the Mayor / chief PM** in this thread. The org builds in the background; between sprints I bring you results and you steer.
- **Safety nets:** clean rollback point committed (`95c1ee5`); the **live VM demo keeps running untouched** during the sprint (I only redeploy after I've reviewed + verified the loop still works).

## While it builds — your input shapes the next sprints:
- **Roadmap priority** after foundation: I have it as Sprint 1 = Jira + Docs, Sprint 2 = Observability v2 + Incidents v2. Want to reorder (e.g. Observability before Jira)?
- **RBAC depth** for enterprise: simple roles (owner/admin/member) for now, or full per-resource permissions?
- **Anything you want the PMs to emphasize** — e.g. a specific Datadog/PagerDuty feature that matters most for the demo?

I'll report back with the Sprint 0 results (PRDs, what passed QA, integration status) the moment it lands, then we redeploy and roll into Sprint 1. Fire away with any direction in the meantime.

**Sprint 2 — Operations (next, highest leverage).** Observability v2 + Incidents v2. This is the single biggest force-multiplier on the crown jewel: instead of "a 500 happened," the demo becomes **real metrics → error-rate monitor fires → PagerDuty-grade incident (severity, on-call, timeline) → autonomous agent fix → auto-written postmortem.** Datadog + PagerDuty quality is exactly what makes judges believe it's real. This is where the "wow" compounds.

**Sprint 3 — The Swarm (the closer).** This is literally one of the hackathon's own thought-starters ("point a team of agents at your real backlog, ship the release"). Wire the platform to **operate itself end-to-end**:
- incident → postmortem auto-filed in **Docs**, follow-up auto-filed in **Jira**, monitor auto-created in **Observability**
- surface the **agent org in-product** (PM/builder/QA agents working a live backlog)
- the killer live moment: **point the swarm at Hull's own Jira backlog and ship a feature on stage**
- fold in the enterprise hardening that makes it credible: **RBAC enforcement, audit log, API keys**

**Then (~last 90 min): harden + dress-rehearse + record the video + submit.** Non-negotiable time box so we don't get caught.

The throughline: every sprint makes the *autonomous loop* look more inevitable, ending with Hull running Hull.

### 🤖 Assistant

🚀 **Maximum parallelism, now running.** `/workflows` to watch.

## What changed (your feedback, applied)
The bottleneck was that I'd treated multitenancy as a *whole serial sprint*. It's actually a small **contract**. So:
1. **I hand-wrote the tenancy contract** (`accounts/`: Org, Membership, `OrgScopedModel` base, current-org middleware, scoping helpers, working auth) — committed (`413e768`), verified live.
2. **Rewrote the harness to fan out 11 workstreams at once** — every section builds in parallel because each owns one disjoint app and imports the shared contract.

## Running now — 11 concurrent workstreams (up to 14 agents at once on your 16-core box):
`accounts` · `projects` · `deploys` (Docker Compose + custom domains) · `agents` · `vcs` · `observability` (Datadog-level) · `orchestration` (agent-org UI) · `issues` (Jira) · `wiki` (Docs) · `oncall` (Incidents v2) · `enterprise` (RBAC/audit/API keys)

Each runs the full loop: **PM** writes a PRD + machine-checkable rubric (generate-and-filter) → **builder** implements → **adversarial QA** verifies and loops until green → then one **integrator** wires shared files, runs all migrations, tests, boots, and **regression-gates the autonomous loop**.

## Guardrails
- Builders never touch shared files or migrate (no races); the contract (`accounts/models.py`) is frozen.
- Clean rollback point (`b2771e9`); the **live VM demo stays up untouched** until I review the results and redeploy.
- Crown-jewel loop is a hard QA gate every workstream is told to preserve.

This is a big fan-out — it'll run a while and burn real tokens (your "aggressive" call). I'll report the full results when it lands: which workstreams passed QA, the integration status, and anything that needs my hands-on cleanup before we redeploy. Keep steering in the meantime — e.g. if you want me to prioritize reviewing any particular section first when it's done.

It's still running, so its data is `org=None`. Let me attach the existing demo data to your **Acme** org so your dashboard is populated when you log in:

**🔧 Bash**

```
cd /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon
source .venv/bin/activate
python manage.py shell -c "
from django.apps import apps
from accounts.models import Org
acme = Org.objects.get(id=9)
total=0
for model in apps.get_models():
    fields=[f.name for f in model._meta.get_fields() if getattr(f,'attname',None)=='org_id']
    if 'org' in [f.name for f in model._meta.fields] and any(f.name=='org' for f in model._meta.fields):
        try:
            n=model.objects.filter(org__isnull=True).update(org=acme)
            if n: print(f'{model._meta.label}: +{n}'); total+=n
        except Exception as e:
            pass
print('reassigned', total, 'records to Acme Inc')
" 2>&1 | tail -25
```

Default OFF (HELM_USE_TEMPORAL=0): the threaded fallback in ``service.py`` runs

## 👤 User

# Update Config Skill

Modify Claude Code configuration by updating settings.json files.

## When Hooks Are Required (Not Memory)

If the user wants something to happen automatically in response to an EVENT, they need a **hook** configured in settings.json. Memory/preferences cannot trigger automated actions.

**These require hooks:**
- "Before compacting, ask me what to preserve" → PreCompact hook
- "After writing files, run prettier" → PostToolUse hook with Write|Edit matcher
- "When I run bash commands, log them" → PreToolUse hook with Bash matcher
- "Always run tests after code changes" → PostToolUse hook

**Hook events:** PreToolUse, PostToolUse, PreCompact, PostCompact, Stop, Notification, SessionStart

## CRITICAL: Read Before Write

**Always read the existing settings file before making changes.** Merge new settings with existing ones - never replace the entire file.

## CRITICAL: Use AskUserQuestion for Ambiguity

When the user's request is ambiguous, use AskUserQuestion to clarify:
- Which settings file to modify (user/project/local)
- Whether to add to existing arrays or replace them
- Specific values when multiple options exist

## Decision: /config command vs Direct Edit

**Suggest the `/config` slash command** for these simple settings:
- `theme`, `editorMode`, `verbose`, `model`
- `language`, `alwaysThinkingEnabled`
- `permissions.defaultMode`

**Edit settings.json directly** for:
- Hooks (PreToolUse, PostToolUse, etc.)
- Complex permission rules (allow/deny arrays)
- Environment variables
- MCP server configuration
- Plugin configuration

566	            append_build("no repo Dockerfile — generated one")
567	
568	        compose_path = compose_rt.write_stack_files(app_dir, compose_spec, dockerfile)
569	        append_build(f"wrote compose spec: {compose_path}")
570	
571	        pname = compose_rt.compose_project_name(project.slug, environment.name)
572	        ok = compose_rt.compose_up(app_dir, compose_path, pname, append_build)
573	        if not ok:
574	            raise RuntimeError("docker compose up failed")
575	
576	        healthy = _health_poll(port, timeout=60.0)
577	        deployment.status = Deployment.Status.LIVE
578	        deployment.health = (
579	            Deployment.Health.HEALTHY if healthy else Deployment.Health.UNKNOWN
580	        )
581	        deployment.live_at = timezone.now()
```

</details>

Root cause: the 52-agent sprint left **orphan app processes squatting on ports**, and a new deploy falsely health-checked **green against a squatter** instead of its own (failed-to-bind) process. Fixes:
1. Killed all orphans + reset stale deployment state (clean slate)
2. **Hardened `_health_poll`** to fail fast when our process dies (failed bind) instead of passing against a squatter — so a deploy can never again report LIVE against the wrong process

---

## Authoritative Answers on Auth Precedence & Switching Billing

### 1. **How Claude Code Decides Between Subscription vs ANTHROPIC_API_KEY**

**Precedence (highest to lowest):**

1. Cloud provider credentials (`CLAUDE_CODE_USE_BEDROCK`, `CLAUDE_CODE_USE_VERTEX`, `CLAUDE_CODE_USE_FOUNDRY`)
2. `ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN` env var (bearer token via gateway/proxy)
3. **`ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` env var** (Anthropic API key)
4. `apiKeyHelper` script output
5. `CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN` env var (long-lived token from `claude setup-token`)
6. Subscription OAuth credentials (from `/login`)

**Critical detail:** If you have BOTH a logged-in subscription AND `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` set, **the API key takes precedence**. However, Claude Code prompts you once in interactive mode to approve the detected key—your choice is remembered. After approval, you can toggle it off via `/config` ("Use custom API key" toggle).

**Gotcha:** If the API key belongs to a disabled/expired organization, auth will fail silently. In that case, run `unset ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` to fall back to your subscription.


… [truncated 4848 chars] …
```

</details>

### 🤖 Assistant

Here's the authoritative answer. Short version: **you can't flip billing on this running process — but you can resume this exact conversation under the API key with a quick restart.**

## How it works
- **Precedence:** `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` (env) outranks subscription login. If both are present, the key wins — but interactive mode prompts **once** ("Use custom API key?"); approve it.
- **Mid-session:** not possible. Env vars are read at startup, so a switch needs a restart. `/login` does *not* change billing mid-session either.

## Steps to switch *and keep this whole conversation*

```bash
# 1. Exit this session (Ctrl+C twice, or /quit). It auto-saves to disk.

# 2. Export the key (it's already in our gitignored env file):
export ANTHROPIC_API_KEY="$(grep '^ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=' ~/dev/claude-hackathon/.env.helm.local | cut -d= -f2-)"

# 3. Resume THIS conversation under the new billing:
cd ~/dev/claude-hackathon && claude --continue
```

`--continue` reopens the most recent session in this directory with full context intact. Approve the one-time API-key prompt, then **`/status`** to confirm it shows *Anthropic Console (API key)*.

## Two notes
1. **Same key already in use for agents:** the autonomous agents/workflows already bill to this API key (we wired `.env.helm.local`). This change only moves *your interactive session*'s tokens onto it too.
2. **Make it permanent** (every future session in any dir) — add to `~/.claude/settings.json`:
   ```json
   { "env": { "ANTHROPIC_API_KEY": "sk-ant-..." } }
   ```
   Shell `export` overrides it, so the export route is fine for just this work.

## Heads-up before you restart

Want me to **commit everything first** so nothing's lost across the restart? I'd recommend yes — say the word and I'll commit, then you can safely Ctrl+C and `claude --continue`.

### 🤖 Assistant

I've audited the demo-critical sections in depth. Here's the honest state-of-the-build and direct answers to your questions — then a proposed sprint for you to steer.

## Your questions, answered

**"How do I make a new deployment?"** → Projects → click a project → an environment card → **Deploy** button (`POST /projects/<slug>/deploy/<env_pk>/`). Importing also auto-deploys staging+prod. There's no standalone "new deployment" page — deployments are per-environment.

**"Clicking Open goes to `/d/11/` (path, not domain, not the EC2 version)"** → Correct, and it's the biggest deploys gap. Host/domain routing was *built but not wired*: there's a `Domain` model, a host-based proxy, and Caddy on-demand-TLS endpoints (`/deploys/tls/ask`, `/hostmap`) — but the host proxy is **never mounted in `helm/urls.py`**, and `environment.public_url` always returns the `/d/<pk>/` path (never the domain). Also you're on **localhost** — the upgraded multitenant build hasn't been redeployed to the EC2 box yet (the VM still runs the old v1).

**"How do I open a PR?"** → You can't manually — PRs are **agent-only** (created automatically when an agent commits in a worktree). You get diff view, Run CI, and Merge, but no "New PR" button.

**"How do I create an incident?"** → Also no manual path — incidents fire **only from auto-detection** (traceback parse or a Monitor breach). Ack/resolve/assign/postmortem all exist; originating one by hand doesn't.

**"Launching an agent should be an interactive chat"** → Today it's **one-shot headless** (`claude -p`) with a live-streaming log (polls every 1.5s) — impressive to watch, but you can't send follow-ups mid-run. True chat needs session continuation (`--resume`) or the SDK.

**Your understanding of "deployment"** → *Aspirationally* yes (compose: web+db+worker+redis). *Actually*: it defaults to a **subprocess** on the **same host** as the control plane, path-routed. Compose mode is fully built but opt-in (set per-env), and nothing runs on a *separate* EC2 — deployments live on the control-plane box.

## Scorecard vs. the vision

| Section | State | Verdict |
|---|---|---|
| **Observability** | Log search/filter, req/error rate, **p50/p95/p99**, dashboards w/ sparklines, **Monitors that fire incidents** — all end-to-end | 🟢 **Datadog-level, genuinely done** |
| **On-call/Incidents** | Schedules, escalation policies, routing, timeline, ack/resolve, postmortems | 🟢 Rich — but ❌ no *manual* "create incident", escalation tick is manual |
| **Deploys** | compose builder + EnvVar injection solid; host-routing/domains/Caddy **built but unwired**; path-only; same-host | 🟡 **Pieces exist, not assembled** |
| **Import→configure** | `git clone` + heuristic detect (**Django/Procfile only**); **no AI** configures the repo; breaks for Rails/Node/Go | 🔴 **Biggest gap vs your #1 demo** |
| **Agents** | one-shot headless, live stream, auto-PR on commit | 🟡 not interactive |
| **VCS** | diff/CI/merge great; **agent-only** PR creation | 🟡 no manual flow |
| Accounts/Issues/Wiki/Enterprise | built, org-scoped, render 200 | 🟢 solid, lower demo priority |

## The headline

Your dream demo — **"import a GitHub repo → an agentic Temporal loop configures a working docker-compose → it deploys to a real domain"** — is the single most valuable thing to build next, and it's mostly *not there yet*: import is dumb heuristics, compose is template-only (no AI, Django-biased), and the domain routing isn't wired. The good news: the agent machinery, compose builder, Temporal wiring, and Caddy endpoints all **exist** — this sprint is about *assembling and AI-enabling* them, not building from zero.

Let me lock the sprint direction with you:

**🔧 AskUserQuestion**

```

```

## 👤 User

Ok what will sprint 2 do?

### 🤖 Assistant

Here's exactly what Sprint 2 will do — 4 parallel workstreams + my integration/redeploy:

## 1. `deploys` — make a deployment a *real* thing (the big one)
- **Compose by default:** when Docker is present, an environment deploys as a **Docker-Compose stack** (web + Postgres + worker + Redis), not a bare subprocess. Process mode stays as the fallback so the autonomous loop never breaks.
- **A real domain per environment:** every deploy auto-provisions a hostname like **`pocketshop-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com`** (the wildcard already points at the EC2 box).
- **Host-based routing:** a new `HostProxyMiddleware` routes by the `Host` header → the right deployment, with **Caddy on-demand TLS**. The `/d/<pk>/` path stays as a fallback (the loop uses it), but **"Open" now takes you to the real `https://…` domain**, not `localhost:8000/d/11/`.

## 2. `vcs` — manual **New PR** flow
A "New PR" form (project + head branch + base + title) so you can open a PR by hand, not only via agents. Diff/CI/merge already work.

## 3. `observability` — manual **Create Incident** flow
A "Declare incident" button (project, severity, title, message) that enters the **same pipeline** as auto-detected ones — fires the on-call timeline/routing and can kick remediation. Lets you trigger the PagerDuty story on demand in the demo.

## 4. `core` — dashboard org-scoping
The Mission Control dashboard will show **only your org's** data (fixes the cross-org leak you'd have seen) + an org-switcher in the nav.

## Then I handle (integration, not agents):
- Wire the new middleware into `settings.py`, run migrations, regression-gate the **autonomous loop**, boot-check.
- **Redeploy the upgraded multitenant Hull to the EC2 box** + reconfigure **Caddy for wildcard on-demand TLS** — so the custom domains actually resolve and serve publicly (they won't resolve on localhost, since the wildcard points at EC2).

## End state for your demo
Import a project → it deploys as a compose stack → click **Open** → land on a real `https://<project>-<env>.apps.dev-reservclaims.com` site. Plus declare incidents and open PRs by hand. **Not** in scope this sprint: the AI import-configure loop (next sprint) and interactive agent chat (deferred).

**Roughly ~6 agents, ~20–30 min**, on the clean `678aa42` rollback point. Want me to launch it?

## You've identified a genuine design flaw
My harness is **sprint-config-driven**: every run, PMs derive a fresh PRD and builders implement the workstream brief *regardless of what already exists*. Your mental model — **agents read repo state + pick the next open ticket from a backlog the PM maintains** — is the correct, simpler, idempotent design. With a backlog, re-running does nothing for already-done tickets. That's what we should have.

Let me confirm the *currently running* Sprint 2 is doing genuinely new work (not another re-run):

## Your critique is the right one, and it's fixable
The root flaw: my harness **re-derives work from a static sprint config** every run, so it's not idempotent — re-running redoes/duplicates work unpredictably. Your model is correct and simpler:

> **A backlog is the source of truth. The PM maintains tickets; a builder picks the next OPEN ticket, does it, marks it DONE. Re-running skips DONE work.**

And we already have the perfect home for that backlog: **the Issues (Jira) app we built** — making the agent backlog live *in the product* is exactly on-vision (PM agents file tickets → builder agents pick them up). That becomes the engine for all future sprints, and it's inherently safe against this class of error.

Two decisions so I don't spend more without your call:

### 🤖 Assistant

Plan set: **let Sprint 2 finish**, then switch to a **file-backlog model**. I'll build that harness now (it's just authoring — zero agent spend — so it's ready the moment Sprint 2 lands).

The design, kept deliberately simple and **idempotent**:
- One file per section: `docs/backlog/<section>.md` with checkbox tickets (`- [ ] DEP-3: …` / `- [x] DEP-1: … (done)`)
- Each section's agent: **(1) Refine** — read the code + backlog, tick off anything already satisfied (so completed work is never redone); **(2) Build** — implement the next 1–2 *open* tickets, tick them when verified; **(3) QA** — adversarially verify, reopen on failure.
- Re-running is safe: done tickets stay done, agents only pick up open ones — exactly your mental model.

Let me write it:

**🔧 Write**

```
/Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon/workflows/backlog.workflow.js
```

        ).first()

    @property
    def public_url(self):
        from django.conf import settings

        return f"{settings.HELM_BASE_URL.rstrip('/')}/d/{self.pk}/"

    @property
    def primary_domain(self):
        """First active custom Domain bound to this env, if any."""
        return self.domains.filter(status=Domain.Status.ACTIVE).order_by(
            "created_at"
        ).first()

55	def _resolve_env_by_host(request):
56	    """Resolve an Environment from the inbound Host header via an ACTIVE
57	    custom Domain. Returns the Environment or None."""
58	    host = (request.get_host() or "").split(":")[0].strip().lower()
59	    if not host:
60	        return None
61	    domain = (
62	        Domain.objects.filter(hostname__iexact=host, status=Domain.Status.ACTIVE)
63	        .select_related("environment", "environment__project")
64	        .first()
65	    )
66	    return domain.environment if domain else None
67	
68	
69	def _proxy_to(request, environment, path):
70	    """Forward the request to the environment's live deployment process."""
71	    deployment = environment.current_deployment
72	    if (

74	        or deployment.status != Deployment.Status.LIVE
75	        or not deployment.port
76	    ):
77	        return _error_page(

=== tls_ask + host_map endpoint logic ===
def tls_ask(request):
    """Caddy ``on_demand_tls { ask <url> }`` allowlist endpoint.

    GET ?domain=<hostname>:
      * 200 if a known ACTIVE Domain matches -> Caddy may issue a cert.
      * 404 otherwise. Never raises.
    """
    host = (request.GET.get("domain") or "").split(":")[0].strip().lower()
    if not host:
        return HttpResponse("missing domain", status=404, content_type="text/plain")
    ok = Domain.objects.filter(
        hostname__iexact=host, status=Domain.Status.ACTIVE
    ).exists()
    if ok:
        return HttpResponse("ok", status=200, content_type="text/plain")
    return HttpResponse("unknown domain", status=404, content_type="text/plain")


def host_map(request):
    """JSON map of active hostname -> upstream local port, for Caddy/ops.
    UNSCOPED (ops integration)."""
    out = {}
    for d in Domain.objects.filter(status=Domain.Status.ACTIVE).select_related(
        "environment"
    ):
        dep = d.environment.current_deployment
        if dep and dep.status == Deployment.Status.LIVE and dep.port:
            out[d
… [truncated 252 chars] …
```

- `parallel-workstreams-backup` → a git **stash** ("index on main" / "WIP on main" are stash messages), not real branch work
- `workstream/observability-v2` → an **older snapshot**; main is a superset
- `agent/fix-inc-*`, `agent/lf-*`, `core-dashboard-iso` → leftover **git worktrees** the remediation/build agents created (the autonomous loop branches per worktree); 0–1 commits, content already on main

So: **everything is merged into main.** `git cherry` shows them as "+" only because they were integrated/squashed differently, not because the work is missing — the tree-level diff confirms main is ahead.

Want me to **prune the stale branches + leftover worktrees** so the repo is clean and unambiguous? It's safe (main is a superset), and it'll prevent any accidental bad merge. I'd keep only `main`.

Separately — the EC2 PocketShop deploy (`b5r4sfz15`) is still finishing; I'll verify the live app domain + loop right after.

### 🤖 Assistant

DB side is perfect — both domains active, `public_url` is the real `https://…`. But the app domain returns `000` (connection failed). Since `hull.dev-reservclaims.com` works on 443, it's specific to the app domain — likely DNS for that subdomain or on-demand TLS issuance. Let me diagnose:

**🔧 Bash**

```
cd /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon
H=pocketshop-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com
echo "=== DNS: does $H resolve? ==="
dig +short $H @8.8.8.8 2>&1 | head
echo "=== tls/ask endpoint approves it? (on the box) ==="
ssh -i .helm_data/hull-demo.pem ubuntu@54.185.134.217 "curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}\n' 'http://127.0.0.1:8000/deploys/tls/ask?domain=$H'" 2>&1
echo "=== bypass DNS, hit the IP directly with SNI (--resolve) ==="
curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}\n" --max-time 25 --resolve $H:443:54.185.134.217 https://$H/ 2>&1
echo "=== recent caddy errors on the box ==="
ssh -i .helm_data/hull-demo.pem ubuntu@54.185.134.217 "sudo journalctl -u caddy --no-pager -n 15 2>/dev/null | grep -iE 'error|on_demand|ask|tls|obtain' | tail -10" 2>&1 | tail -10
```

```

Jun 13 21:16:24 ip-10-1-21-165 caddy[6643]: {"level":"error","ts":1781385384.4443948,"logger":"tls","msg":"failed to get permission for on-demand certificate","domain":"pocketshop-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com","error":"checking http://127.0.0.1:8000/deploys/tls/ask to determine if certificate for hostname 'pocketshop-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com' should be allowed: Get \"/deploys/tls/ask/?domain=pocketshop-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com\": following http redi
… [truncated 3940 chars] …
```

</details>

### 🤖 Assistant

Nailed it. The `tls/ask` endpoint returns **301** (Django's `APPEND_SLASH` adds the trailing slash), and **Caddy refuses to follow redirects** on the ask check → on-demand cert denied → TLS fails → `000`. The Caddy config asks `…/tls/ask` but the Django route is `…/tls/ask/`. 

One-char fix (trailing slash). Let me patch the live Caddyfile + fix `remote_setup.sh` for future deploys:

**🔧 Edit**

```
/Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon/deploy/remote_setup.sh
```

<details><summary>tool result</summary>

```
The file /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon/deploy/remote_setup.sh has been updated successfully. (file state is current in your context — no need to Read it back)
```

</details>

**🔧 Bash**

```
cd /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon
echo "=== patch live Caddyfile (add trailing slash) + reload ==="
ssh -i .helm_data/hull-demo.pem ubuntu@54.185.134.217 "sudo sed -i 's#ask http://127.0.0.1:8000/deploys/tls/ask\$#ask http://127.0.0.1:8000/deploys/tls/ask/#' /etc/caddy/Caddyfile && sudo systemctl reload caddy && echo reloaded && grep ask /etc/caddy/Caddyfile" 2>&1
echo "=== retry app domain over HTTPS (cert issues on first hit) ==="
for i in 1 2 3 4; do
  code=$(curl -s -o /tmp/app.html -w "%{http_code}" --max-time 35 https://pocketshop-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com/ 2>/dev/null)
  echo "  attempt $i: $code$([ "$code" = 200 ] && echo '  storefront:'$(grep -oc PocketShop /tmp/app.html))"
  [ "$code" = "200" ] && break
  sleep 4
done
```

## Gold demo — beat-by-beat gap analysis

| # | Demo beat | Status | What exists today | Gap to close |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | **Import → agentic loop configures & deploys** | 🔴 **Biggest gap** | Import = `git clone` + *heuristic* detect (Django `manage.py` / Procfile / `package.json` only). Deploy works (compose-when-docker / process) + auto custom domain. | **No agent in the loop.** Need: an agent that inspects the repo, writes a working Dockerfile/compose, validates it builds, commits — general across **Rails/Go/Node/etc** (today only Django really works). Wrap in Temporal. |
| 2 | Check out the deployed product | 🟢 **Ready** | `https://<proj>-<env>.apps.dev-reservclaims.com/` live w/ TLS (verified) | — |
| 3 | New feature branch | 🟢 Ready | Launching an agent auto-creates a worktree on a branch | (optional) explicit "new branch" UI |
| 4 | **Create Ticket → launch workspace + agent autonomously** | 🟠 **Partial** | Issues (Jira) app: boards/tickets exist. Agents launch from `/agents/new/`. | **No ticket→agent linkage.** Need a "Work this ticket" button: ticket → create worktree → launch agent, status flips to in-progress, links the resulting PR back to the ticket. |
| 5 | Launch a few more, watch the **agent observability dashboard** | 🟠 Partial | Agents list + roster + live console; orchestration "Agent Org" run list/detail | Need a **single live multi-agent dashboard** (all active agents, streaming status/cost/turns at a glance). Pieces exist; needs a unified view + polish. |
| 6 | Create PRs, review, merge | 🟢 Ready | Agent + manual PRs; diff, CI, merge button | — |
| 7 | Deploy | 🟢 Ready | Merge auto-triggers redeploy of the tracking env (`_maybe_redeploy`) | — |
| 8 | Check it out in production | 🟢 Ready | Prod domain serves | — |
| 9 | Trigger an error | 🟢 Ready | PocketShop `BOGO` planted bug → 500 (deterministic) | (optional) manual "Declare incident" for non-bug triggers |
| 10 | Incidents/agents — **already working on a solution** | 🟢 **Ready (crown jewel)** | Error → auto-incident (traceback/monitor) → auto-remediation agent → incident page shows it live | Verify live on EC2 (1 run) |
| 11 | Check remediation PR, review, merge | 🟢 Ready | Remediation PR + CI + merge | — |
| 12 | Deploy → works now | 🟢 Ready | Auto-merge + redeploy → prod healed (BOGO→200) | — |
| 13 | Show logging, on-call, analytics | 🟢 Ready (built) | Datadog-grade obs (log search, p50/95/99, dashboards, monitors); PagerDuty-grade on-call (schedules/escalation/timeline/postmortems) | Ensure they're **populated** for the demo |

## The verdict
**The back half of the demo (beats 6–13: PR→deploy→error→autonomous fix→ship) is solid and largely live.** The gaps are concentrated in the **front half** — the two *proactive* agentic moments:

### Critical path to the gold demo (in priority order)
1. **🔴 Agentic import→configure→deploy loop** *(the headline; biggest effort)* — broaden detection (Gemfile/go.mod/pyproject), add a Temporal-run **configure agent** (inspect repo → generate+validate Dockerfile/compose → commit → deploy), plus a deploy-failure→agent-fix retry. This is what makes "import any repo" real.
2. **🟠 Ticket → workspace → agent** *(small-medium)* — a "Work this ticket" action wiring Issues → `agents.services.launch_agent` → PR linked back to the ticket. Makes beat #4 real and showcases the swarm.
3. **🟠 Unified agent observability dashboard** *(polish)* — one live view of all agents working at once (beat #5).
4. **🟢 Demo-readiness** — verify the autonomous loop live on EC2 (1 agent run), seed clean demo data, and (for a *non*-Django live import) make sure a second sample repo configures cleanly.

Optional nice-to-have: manual "Declare incident" (beat #9 alt).

## 👤 User

ok, lets design a new sprint to address these issues and get us to our goal star demo.

### 🤖 Assistant

Here's the proposed **Sprint 3 — "The Gold Demo"**, scoped directly to the gaps and built on the idempotent backlog model.

## Workstreams

**1. 🔴 `import-loop` — agentic import→configure→deploy** *(the centerpiece)*
- Broaden detection: `Gemfile`→Rails, `go.mod`→Go, `package.json`→Node, `pyproject.toml`→Python (today: Django/Procfile only)
- After clone, if the repo lacks a Dockerfile/compose, launch a **configure agent** (reuses `agents.services.launch_agent`): *inspect repo → generate a working Dockerfile + compose → verify it builds → commit* — then deploy. On deploy failure, a **fix agent** retries with the build logs.
- Routed through **Temporal** (`ConfigureProjectWorkflow`), visible in the orchestration UI.
- **Rubric (strict, adversarial):** importing a **non-Django** repo yields a committed Dockerfile/compose **and a LIVE deployment returning 200.**

**2. 🟠 `issues` — ticket → workspace → agent**
- "Work this ticket" button → creates a worktree + launches an agent with the ticket as the brief; ticket flips to in-progress→done; resulting **PR links back to the ticket.**

**3. 🟠 `orchestration` — unified agent observability dashboard**
- One live view of **all agents at once** (status, cost, turns, current action, streaming) — the "swarm" beat.

**4. 🟢 `observability` — manual "Declare incident"** (the missed Sprint 2 item) + ensure analytics/logs are populated for the demo.

**5. 🟢 `sample-app` — a second, non-Django sample repo** to prove "import *any* repo" live.

Plus **demo-readiness (me):** verify the autonomous loop live on EC2, seed clean demo data, refresh `DEMO_SCRIPT.md`.

## The one real infra implication
To deploy a **non-Django** app live (beat #1), its container needs that runtime (Ruby/Node) — which means **Docker on the EC2 box** (compose mode). Today the box runs apps as subprocesses (Django-only). So a true "import a Rails app → it deploys" demo requires installing Docker on EC2.

Two decisions to lock the sprint:

**🔧 AskUserQuestion**

## Sprint 3 — "Gold Demo" (6 parallel workstreams, backlog-driven)

| Section | What it builds |
|---|---|
| **`projects`** | **Simplified import** (require `docker-compose.yml` / `Procfile` / Django `manage.py` — no AI guessing) + the ⭐ **live import progress display**: Clone → Detect → Verify → Domain → Deploy staging → Deploy prod, animated/HTMX-polled |
| **`sample-app`** | **NodeShop** (Node/Express, ships a Procfile **and** compose) to prove "import any repo" beyond Django |
| **`issues`** | **"Work this ticket"** → spins a worktree + launches an agent; resulting PR links back to the ticket |
| **`orchestration`** | **Agent observability dashboard** — the whole swarm live (status/cost/turns/action) |
| **`observability`** | Manual **"Declare incident"** |
| **`design`** | **Warmer color palette** (warm-dark, amber/coral accent) + **bulletproof input styling** (every field type + `class="input"`) |

Captured the full target in **`docs/TARGET_DEMO.md`**; each workstream has a seeded, machine-checkable ticket list in `docs/backlog/`.

**After it runs (mayor-owned):** install Docker on EC2, adversarially verify the import-loop + autonomous loop live, seed clean demo data, refresh the demo script.

## Notes before you confirm
- It's **6 concurrent workstreams** with build→adversarial-QA→loop + integrator — a real chunk of tokens/time (the `projects` QA will actually import NodeShop + docker-build locally, which is heavy but proves it).
- Idempotent: it ticks off anything already done, so re-running is safe.
- Clean rollback point: `ff40ee9`. Live VM untouched until I redeploy.

**Say the word and I'll launch it.** Or tweak any workstream first (e.g., palette direction — amber vs coral vs terracotta — if you have a preference, I'll bake it into the design ticket).

## 👤 User

how much can you interact with the running workflow? can you see what it is doing right now

### 🤖 Assistant

Good question. Here's the honest interaction model, then a live peek (I can actually see quite a bit):

**What I can/can't do with a running workflow:**
- ❌ I **can't** pause, step, or message it mid-run, or interactively steer individual agents. It runs to completion in the background; I get a notification when done.
- ✅ I **can stop** it (`TaskStop`) — that's the only direct control.
- ✅ I **can observe** it live indirectly: the agents update `docs/backlog/*.md` (ticking tickets `[x]` with evidence), and edit files in the tree — so reading those shows real-time progress. (I avoid reading the raw agent transcripts — they'd blow up my context.)
- ✅ **You** get the best live view via `/workflows` (the progress tree).

Let me show you what it's doing **right now**:

## 👤 User

lets do some quick testing on our local first. on mission control, i see 2 projects and 5 deploys but on the projects tab i see 0 and only 3 deploys on deployments tab

### 🤖 Assistant

Good catch — that's an **org-scoping inconsistency**: the dashboard uses an OR policy (shows your org **+** unscoped `org=None` loop/demo data), but the Projects/Deploys tabs use **strict** `for_org` (hides `org=None`). So demo data created by the import/loop (which has `org=None`) shows on the dashboard but vanishes in the tabs. Let me confirm the diagnosis:

1	"""Helpers builders use to enforce org scoping in views.  [stable contract]
2	
3	Usage in a view::
4	
5	    from accounts.scoping import org_required, scoped
6	
7	    @org_required
8	    def my_list(request):
9	        items = scoped(MyModel, request)          # filtered to request.org
10	        ...
11	
12	For models that subclass ``OrgScopedModel`` you can also use

16	from functools import wraps

18	from django.contrib.auth.decorators import login_required
19	from django.shortcuts import redirect

21	
22	def org_required(view):
23	    """login_required + ensures the user has an active org (else onboarding)."""
24	
25	    @wraps(view)
26	    @login_required
27	    def _wrapped(request, *args, **kwargs):
28	        if getattr(request, "org", None) is None:
29	            return redirect("accounts:onboarding")
30	        return view(request, *args, **kwargs)
31	
32	    return _wrapped

39	    """
40	    qs = model_or_qs if hasattr(model_
… [truncated 241 chars] …

def deploy_detail(request, pk):
    deployment = get_object_or_404(
        scoped(Deployment, request).select_related(
            "environment", "environment__project"
        ),
        pk=pk,
    )
    return render(request, "deploys/detail.html", {"deployment": deployment})

## 👤 User

ok, walk me through importing a project. first install docker on the box of course

### 🤖 Assistant

Let me install Docker on the box (and bake it into `remote_setup.sh` for future deploys), then I'll walk you through the import.

**🔧 Bash**

```
cd /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon
echo "=== installing Docker on EC2 (official script) ==="
ssh -i .helm_data/hull-demo.pem -o StrictHostKeyChecking=accept-new ubuntu@54.185.134.217 "
  if command -v docker >/dev/null; then echo 'docker already present'; else
    curl -fsSL https://get.docker.com | sudo sh >/tmp/docker-install.log 2>&1 && echo 'docker installed';
  fi
  sudo usermod -aG docker ubuntu
  sudo systemctl enable --now docker
  docker --version
  sudo docker compose version 2>/dev/null | head -1 || echo 'compose plugin: checking'
  # restart helm so the gunicorn (ubuntu) process gains the docker group
  sudo systemctl restart helm && echo 'helm restarted'
" 2>&1 | tail -12
```

### 🤖 Assistant

17 files use `{#` (several multi-line — those are the broken ones). I'll convert them all to `{% comment %}…{% endcomment %}` (handles single + multi-line) via a DOTALL regex:

**🔧 Bash**

```
cd /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon
python3 - <<'PY'
import re, pathlib, subprocess
files = subprocess.check_output(
    "grep -rln '{#' --include='*.html' . | grep -vE '\\.venv|\\.helm_data|sample_apps|staticfiles'",
    shell=True, text=True).split()
pat = re.compile(r'\{#(.*?)#\}', re.S)
changed=0
for f in files:
    p=pathlib.Path(f); t=p.read_text()
    n=len(pat.findall(t))
    if n:
        t2=pat.sub(lambda m: '{% comment %}'+m.group(1)+'{% endcomment %}', t)
        p.write_text(t2); changed+=1; print(f"  {f}: {n} comment(s) converted")
print("files changed:", changed)
PY
echo "=== verify no {# remains in Hull templates ==="
grep -rn "{#" --include="*.html" . 2>/dev/null | grep -vE "\.venv|\.helm_data|sample_apps|staticfiles" | wc -l | tr -d ' '
echo "=== django check (catches unbalanced comment tags) ==="
source .venv/bin/activate; python manage.py check 2>&1 | tail -2
```

### 🤖 Assistant

Box is clean (only PocketShop remains; test containers removed). Everything's verified and live. **Here's your import walkthrough:**

## Importing a project on https://hull.dev-reservclaims.com

1. **Log in** → `demo` / `demo12345`
2. **Projects** (sidebar) → **"+ Import project"**
3. Fill in:
   - **Name:** `WidgetCart`
   - **Repo URL:** `/home/ubuntu/helm/sample_apps/widgetcart`
     *(the bundled Node/Express sample on the box — ships a Procfile + docker-compose. Any repo with a `docker-compose.yml`, `Procfile`, or Django `manage.py` works; an unsupported repo fails fast with a clear message.)*
4. **Submit** → you land on the project page and the **live import stepper** animates:
   **Clone → Detect runtime (`compose`) → Verify environment → Provision domain → Deploy staging → Deploy prod** (pending → running → done, ~30s; Node compose build is fast)
5. When the env cards go **live**, click **Open** on prod → loads at **`https://widgetcart-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com/`** (real custom domain, on-demand TLS, host-routed)

What's happening under the hood: Hull clones the repo, detects it declares `compose`, stamps the envs as compose-runtime, **builds + runs the Docker-Compose stack** (web + db + redis + worker), provisions the hostname, and brings up staging then prod — all surfaced live in the stepper.

**Note:** that repo field is a server-side path (works today). If you'd rather demo a real **`github.com/...`** URL, say the word and I'll push WidgetCart to a public GitHub repo (~1 min) so the import reads a true GitHub link.

Go ahead and run it — tell me what you see and I'll fix anything live.

=== #1 import redirect: project_new flow ===
def project_new(request):
    if request.method == "POST":
        name = (request.POST.get("name") or "").strip()
        repo_url = (request.POST.get("repo_url") or "").strip()
        description = (request.POST.get("description") or "").strip()
        if not name or not repo_url:
            messages.error(request, "Name and repository URL are required.")
            return render(
                request,
                "projects/new.html",
                {"name": name, "repo_url": repo_url, "description": description},
            )

        # Tag the import with the acting user's active org so the created
        # Project is scoped to their tenant.
        org = getattr(request, "org", None)
        threading.Thread(
            target=_import_in_background,
            args=(name, repo_url, description),
            kwargs={"org": org},
            daemon=True,
        ).start()
        messages.success(request, f"Importing {name}… this runs in the background.")
        return redirect(reverse("projects:list"))

def _import_in_background(name, repo_url, description, *, org=None):
    """Prefer orchestration.import_project (which also auto-deploys). If that
    raises NotImplementedError, fall back to projects.services.import_project +
    auto-deploy each environment via deploys.services.deploy.

    ``org`` tags the created Project with the acting tenant. We try to pass it
    to orchestration if that layer accepts it (additive kwarg); if not, we fall
    back to the direct service path which always honors ``org`` — this keeps the
    autonomous loop's existing org-less behavior intact while guaranteeing UI
    imports are org-tagged."""

250	def _tee_output(deployment, popen, log_path):
251	    """Daemon-thread target: read process output line by line, write to the log
252	    file, and stream each line to observability.services.ingest_line."""
253	    from observability import services as obs
254	
255	    try:
256	        with open(log_path, "a", encoding="utf-8", errors="replace") as logf:
257	            for raw in iter(popen.stdout.readline, ""):
258	                if raw == "":
259	                    break
260	                logf.write(raw)
261	                logf.flush()
262	                line = raw.rstrip("\n")
263	                try:
264	                    obs.ingest_line(deployment, line)
265	                except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — ingest must never kill deploy
266	                    pass
267	    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001
268	        pass
269

33	def _ensure_domain(environment):
34	    """Give an environment a stable real hostname (idempotent), so it's reachable

435:def _ensure_local_git_repo(repo_url: str) -> None:
def _ensure_local_git_repo(repo_url: str) -> None:
    """If ``repo_url`` is a local directory that isn't yet a git repo,
    initialize one and commit its contents so Hull can clone it.

    This lets a plain source tree (e.g. the bundled sample app, tracked as
    normal files in Hull's own repo) be imported without shipping a nested
    .git. Idempotent and a no-op for URLs / existing repos.
    """
    if "://" in repo_url and not repo_url.startswith("file://"):
        return
    path = repo_url[len("file://"):] if repo_url.startswith("file://") else repo_url
    if not os.path.isdir(path) or os.path.isdir(os.path.join(path, ".git")):
        return
    env = {**os.environ, "GIT_AUTHOR_NAME": "Hull", "GIT_AUTHOR_EMAIL": "helm@helm.dev",
           "GIT_COMMITTER_NAME": "Hull", "GIT_COMMITTER_EMAIL": "helm@helm.dev"}
    subprocess.run(["git", "init", "-b", "main"], cwd=path, env=env,
                   stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.STDOUT, text=True)
    subprocess.run(["git", "add", "-A"], cwd=path, env=env,
                   stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.STDOUT, text=True)
    subprocess.run(["gi
… [truncated 220 chars] …
```

@org_required
def project_delete(request, slug):
    """Delete a project: stop its deployments (process + compose), then remove it
    (cascades envs/deployments/domains/incidents/agent runs). Demo-friendly reset.
    """
    project = get_object_or_404(visible(Project, request), slug=slug)
    if request.method != "POST":
        return redirect(project.get_absolute_url())

    import subprocess as _sp

    from deploys import services as deploy_services

    for env in project.environments.all():
        for dep in env.deployments.all():
            try:
                deploy_services.stop(dep)
            except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001
                pass
        # Best-effort compose teardown by project name (no file needed).
        try:
            from deploys.compose.runtime import compose_project_name

 
… [truncated 989 chars] …

### 🤖 Assistant

The widgetcart sample has a **nested `.git`** with a stale HEAD (no `/boom`), and my edits are uncommitted inside it. The main repo also tracks these files. The cleanest fix is to remove the nested `.git` so widgetcart is just part of the main repo — then imports pick up the actual on-disk `server.js`:

**🔧 Bash**

```
cd /Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon
# Remove the nested git repo so widgetcart is plain files in the main repo.
rm -rf sample_apps/widgetcart/.git
echo "=== removed nested .git ==="
git -C sample_apps/widgetcart status 2>&1 | head -2 || true
echo "=== on-disk server.js has /boom + logging? ==="
grep -c "/boom" sample_apps/widgetcart/server.js
grep -c "accessLog" sample_apps/widgetcart/server.js
echo "=== main repo now sees server.js modified? ==="
git status --short sample_apps/widgetcart/
```

#!/usr/bin/env python
"""Import the WidgetCart Node sample into Hull and assert a LIVE HTTP 200.

PROJECTS-4 acceptance: importing a non-Django sample that ships a Procfile +
docker-compose.yml runs the full import pipeline and yields a live deployment
returning HTTP 200 (via Docker Compose when Docker is present, else the process
runtime running ``node server.js``).

Run from the repo root with the project's venv active::

    python sample_apps/widgetcart/import_widgetcart.py

Exits 0 on a live 200, non-zero (with a reason) otherwise. Skips cleanly with a
clear message if Node is unavailable on this box.

435	def _ensure_local_git_repo(repo_url: str) -> None:
436	    """If ``repo_url`` is a local directory that isn't yet a git repo,
437	    initialize one and commit its contents so Hull can clone it.
438	
439	    This lets a plain source tree (e.g. the bundled sample app, tracked as

295	def _tee_compose_logs(deployment_pk, app_dir, compose_path, project_name, log_path):
296	    """Follow a compose stack's container logs and stream each line into Hull's
297	    observability ingestion (LogLines + metrics + monitors), so Docker-Compose
298	    deployments are as observable as the process runtime. Resolves the deployment
299	    by pk each line so it's safe across threads. Best-effort."""
300	    from observability import services as obs
301	
302	    cmd = [
303	        "docker", "compose", "-p", project_name, "-f", compose_path,
304	        "logs", "-f", "--no-color", "--no-log-prefix", "--tail", "0",
305	    ]
306	    try:
307	        proc = subprocess.Popen(
308	            cmd, cwd=app_dir, stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.STDOUT,
309	            text=True, bufsize=1,
310	        )
311	    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001
312	        return
313	    _PROCS[f"compose-logs-{deployment_pk}"] = proc
314	    try:
315	        with open(log_path, "a", encoding="utf-8", errors="replace") as logf:
316	            for raw in iter(proc.stdout.readline, ""):
317	                if raw == "":
318	                    break

#!/usr/bin/env bash
# Lightweight code sync to the live EC2 box for small fixes: rsync code,
# collectstatic, restart gunicorn. Does NOT reinstall deps, touch the DB, or
# reconfigure Caddy (use deploy/push.sh for a full provision). Fast iteration.
#
#   ./deploy/sync.sh ubuntu@54.185.134.217 .helm_data/hull-demo.pem
set -euo pipefail

REMOTE="${1:?usage: sync.sh user@host [ssh-key]}"
KEY="${2:-}"
SSH_OPTS="-o StrictHostKeyChecking=accept-new"
[ -n "$KEY" ] && SSH_OPTS="$SSH_OPTS -i $KEY"
DIR="helm"

here="$(cd "$(dirname "$0")/.." && pwd)"; cd "$here"

echo "▸ rsync code -> ${REMOTE}:~/${DIR}"
rsync -az \
  --exclude '.venv/' --exclude '.helm_data/' --exclude '*.sqlite3*' \
  --exclude '__pycache__/' --exclude '.git/' --exclude 'staticfiles/' \
  --exclude 'node_modules/' --exclude '*.log' --exclude '.env' \
  -e "ssh ${SSH_OPTS}" ./ "${REMOTE}:${DIR}/"

echo "▸ migrate (no-op if none) + collectstatic + restart"
ssh ${SSH_OPTS} "${REMOTE}" "cd ~/${DIR} && source .venv/bin/activate && set -a && source .env && set +a && \
```

# ⎈ Hull — the autonomous software operating system

> One control plane for your entire stack — version control, CI/CD, deployments,

# Hull — the autonomous software operating system

## The problem

Shipping and *operating* a production web app today means stitching together a
pile of disconnected SaaS: GitHub for code and PRs, Vercel/Render for deploys,
PagerDuty/Opsgenie for on-call, Datadog/Sentry for logs and errors, plus the
human glue that ties them together at 3am. Elite individual developers and small
teams pay this "operations tax" disproportionately — they have production
responsibilities but no platform team. When prod breaks, a human has to notice
the alert, find the error, reproduce it, write the fix, open a PR, wait for CI,
merge, and redeploy. Every one of those steps is a place to lose hours.

## The vision

**Hull is one control plane that unifies version control, CI/CD, deployments,
observability, and incident response — and runs it autonomously with a crew of
Claude Opus 4.8 agents.** You import a repo once. Hull deploys it to staging and
prod, watches it, and when production throws an error, Hull doesn't page a
human — it opens an incident, spawns a Claude agent in an isolated git 
… [truncated 4116 chars] …

### 🤖 Assistant

Done. Submission answers are written, committed, and pushed to the public repo (also rendered at the repo root as [`SUBMISSION.md`](https://github.com/jhmaddox/hull-claude-build-day/blob/main/SUBMISSION.md)). Here they are, ready to paste into the form:

---

### Project Description
**Hull is one control plane that unifies version control, CI/CD, deployments, observability, and incident response — and operates it autonomously with a crew of Claude Opus 4.8 agents.** It's GitHub + Vercel + PagerDuty + Datadog fused into a single product, run by agents instead of by you. Import a repo once; Hull detects the runtime, stands up staging + prod with real public URLs, and watches it. Ship features by handing a ticket to an agent that works in an isolated git worktree → opens a PR in Hull's own diff UI → runs CI → spins a preview env. The money shot: a production error is detected from live logs → a PagerDuty-style incident opens → a Claude agent reproduces it, fixes the root cause, adds a regression test, opens a PR, passes CI → human approves the merge (HITL by default) → redeploy → resolved. Built solo at Claude Build Day; Django 5.1 + HTMX, Temporal (threaded fallback), multi-tenant, live on EC2.

### How Opus 4.8 was used
Two ways. **(1) As the runtime engine of the product** — Hull's agents *are* Opus 4.8 (`HELM_AGENT_MODEL=claude-opus-4-8`, headless `claude` CLI in stream-json, each in its own git worktree). Opus does the engineering the product automates: feature agents (ticket → code + tests → PR) and remediation agents (read traceback/logs → locate suspect file → reproduce → fix → add regression test → PR → CI). Reasoning streams live into the UI. **(2) As the builder** — the whole codebase was built by Opus 4.8 via Claude Code, orchestrated by the Workflow scripts below.

### Public GitHub repo
**https://github.com/jhmaddox/hull-claude-build-day**

### How I orchestrated Claude's work
"The Mayor and the build org": I drove the main thread as chief PM and dispatched subagent fleets through deterministic **Workflow scripts**, with the governing rule that *"done" must be model-verifiable with no human in the loop* — a responding URL + a green rubric. Scaffolding: [`CONTRACTS.md`](https://github.com/jhmaddox/hull-claude-build-day/blob/main/CONTRACTS.md) (frozen data model + service signatures + disjoint-dir rules that make fan-out safe), [`brief.md`](https://github.com/jhmaddox/hull-claude-build-day/blob/main/brief.md), and [`rubric.md`](https://github.com/jhmaddox/hull-claude-build-day/blob/main/rubric.md) (a 100-pt machine-checkable rubric a grader agent runs against the live system — the loop's termination condition). Pipelines in [`workflows/`](https://github.com/jhmaddox/hull-claude-build-day/tree/main/workflows): `build_helm.workflow.js` (foundation → 4 parallel slices → integrate → grade-against-rubric loop), `sprint.workflow.js` (PM → parallel builders → adversarial QA → synthesize), `backlog.workflow.js` (idempotent refine → build → QA → integrate). Patterns: contract-first fan-out, generate-and-filter, adversarial verification, loop-until-rubric-green, fan-out & synthesize, idempotent backlogs.

---

A few things worth noting:
- The **live URL** in the docs is `https://hull.dev-reservclaims.com` — make sure the box is up when judges click (it was responding 302→login a few minutes ago).
- I corrected the old `SUBMISSION.md` which had a stale `sslip.io` URL and a placeholder repo link.

import os
os.environ.setdefault("DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE","helm.settings")
import django; django.setup()

def _run(name, fn, *, project=None, ref_type="", ref_id=None, temporal=None,
         on_done=None):
    """Create a WorkflowRun, run ``fn`` in the background, record the outcome.

    ``fn`` is a zero-arg callable that performs the actual work (thread path).
    ``temporal`` (optional) = (workflow_class_name, args_list): when Temporal is
    enabled and reachable, the workflow is started on the cluster and its result
    is awaited (the work runs in the worker, NOT here) — so it's durable and
    visible in Temporal Cloud. If Temporal is unavailable or the start fails, we
    fall back to running ``fn`` on a daemon thread. The WorkflowRun + a
    core.Event are updated on completion / failure.

    ``on_done`` (optional): a zero-arg callable invoked once the run reaches a
    terminal state, on EITHER the threaded OR the Temporal path. Used e.g. by
    ``remediate`` to release its per-incident re-entrancy lock so the durable
    path (where ``fn`` runs in a remote worker, not here) can't leak it. Wrapped
    so a failing callback never disturbs the loop.

    Returns the WorkflowRun immediately.

### 🤖 Assistant

**Found the real bug** — not SQLite. The WorkflowRun for the import shows:

```
UnboundLocalError: cannot access local variable
File "orchestration/service.py", line 236, in _do
    name, repo_url, description=description, org=org, project=project
```

In `import_project._do`, the line `project = project_` makes `project` a **local** variable for the whole function, so the earlier `project=project` argument hits it *before assignment* → `UnboundLocalError`. The work dies instantly in the `_body` thread, leaving the project stuck `importing` forever. This is a regression I introduced in the import-redirect refactor (d50523f) — and it was never caught because I tested `proj_svc.import_project` directly, not through the orchestration `_do` path. Let me fix it:

**🔧 Read**

```
/Users/james/dev/claude-hackathon/orchestration/service.py
```

Fixed and verified end-to-end. 

## What was wrong
Not a cleanup issue — a **real code bug I introduced** in the import-redirect refactor (d50523f). In `orchestration/service.py`, the inner `_do()` did `project = project_`, which made `project` a function-local for the whole closure. So the earlier `project=project` argument to `proj_svc.import_project(...)` hit the variable *before assignment* → `UnboundLocalError`.

The work died instantly inside the background thread, so the Project sat at `status=importing` with every import step stuck `pending` — exactly the "hang" you saw. It slipped through because I'd tested `proj_svc.import_project` directly, never the orchestration `_do` path that the UI actually uses. The proof was in the failed WorkflowRun's traceback on the box.

## The fix
Renamed the result local to `imported` so it never shadows the `project` parameter. Committed (`35fb450`), pushed to the public repo, and synced to EC2.

## Verified on production
- **Real orchestration import path** (the broken one) now runs clean: `ready`, framework `compose`, all 6 steps `done`.
- Cleaned up the stuck `widgetcart` (id 4) + leftover repo dirs + my `wcdiag` test project.
- Reimported WidgetCart end-to-end — **staging + prod both live, HTTP 200** locally *and* via public domains:
  - https://widgetcart-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com/ → 200
  - https://widgetcart-staging.apps.dev-reservclaims.com/ → 200

So WidgetCart is back, imported and serving, and importing through the UI works again. One cosmetic note: the compose `worker` container restart-loops (the generated worker runs `python` against the Node image) — harmless, the web container is what serves, but I can suppress the generated worker for non-Python frameworks if you want it clean for the demo.

---

224	@org_required
225	def import_steps_fragment(request, slug):
226	    """HTMX-polled fragment: the live import-progress stepper for a project.
227	
228	    Org-scoped (404 cross-tenant). Returns just the stepper markup so the detail
229	    page can poll it (~1.5s) and animate pending -> running -> done/failed. When
230	    no steps are in flight it stops self-polling (the wrapper drops hx-trigger)."""
231	    project = get_object_or_404(
232	        visible(Project, request), slug=slug
233	    )
234	    steps = list(project.import_steps.all())
235	    return render(
236	        request,
237	        "projects/_import_steps.html",
238	        {
239	            "project": project,
240	            "import_steps": steps,
241	            "import_active": _import_in_progress(steps),
242	        },
243	    )
```

## Summary of this batch

All five items are done, committed, pushed to the public repo, and live on EC2:

**1. Marketing splash page** — anonymous visitors to `https://hull.dev-reservclaims.com/` now get a polished landing page (`core/landing.html`): hero, the autonomous loop as a 6-step flow, a feature grid framing it against GitHub/Vercel/PagerDuty/Datadog, and sign-in / get-started CTAs. Signed-in users still get Mission Control. Verified live (200, no app chrome).

**2. Repositioned the product** — dropped "autonomous software operating system" (the OS confusion you flagged) for **"the AI-native control plane for software teams"** across the tagline (sidebar, login, title), README, brief, CONTRACTS, and SUBMISSION.

**3. Killed "money shot"** — now "the autonomous loop" (headers) / "flagship demo" (prose). Verified zero occurrences on the live page.

**4. Import auto-refresh** — the import-steps poll now returns `HX-Refresh: true` on the active→settled transition, so environments, deployments, and the status badge appear automatically when an import finishes — no manual refresh.

**5. Empty agent dropdown** — same org-scoping class of bug we hit before: `agents/views` used strict `scoped()`/`for_org()` while the demo projects carry `org=None`. Switched Project + AgentRun queries to `visible()` (current-org **or** shared `org=None`), matching everywhere else. Now both projects show.

One note: that `org=None` on the demo projects is the recurring root cause behind these "I should see N but see 0" bugs. The `visible()` policy handles it everywhere now, but if you'd rather, I can stamp the seeded demo projects with the Acme org so even strict scoping works — say the word.

### 🤖 Assistant

The user wants thoroughness, but I have to be careful: `visible()` only scopes models with a direct `org`/`project` field — for deeper paths (EnvVar/Domain via `environment__project__org`) it would return **unscoped** (a tenant-isolation leak). Let me read the scoping helpers to do this safely:

**🔧 Read**

```

1	"""Helpers builders use to enforce org scoping in views.  [stable contract]
2	
3	Usage in a view::
4	
5	    from accounts.scoping import org_required, scoped
6	
7	    @org_required
8	    def my_list(request):
9	        items = scoped(MyModel, request)          # filtered to request.org

21

23	    """login_required + ensures the user has an active org (else onboarding)."""
24	
25	    @wraps(view)
26	    @login_required
27	    def _wrapped(request, *args, **kwargs):
28	        if getattr(request, "org", None) is None:
29	            return redirect("accounts:onboarding")
30	        return view(request, *args, **kwargs)
31	
32	    return _wrapped

39	    """
40	    qs = model_or_qs if hasattr(model_

=== _env_vars_for + how injected into process popen ===
def _env_vars_for(environment) -> dict:
    """Collect this environment's EnvVar rows (key -> raw value) for deploy-time
    injection into the running app. Raw secret values are used here only — never
    rendered in a read response."""
    out: dict[str, str] = {}
    try:
        for ev in environment.env_vars.all():
            if ev.key:
                out[ev.key] = ev.value or ""
    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — never let config reads break a deploy
        pass
    return out

## 1. Org-scoping sweep (the recurring bug class) — eliminated
Swept every view across **orchestration, vcs, issues, oncall, deploys, wiki, enterprise** (plus the earlier agents + observability) from strict `scoped()`/`for_org()` to `visible()` (current org **or** shared `org=None`). Confirmed safe first: every shared model has a direct `org` field, so `visible()` never falls back to unscoped. Left `accounts` Membership/Invitation strict (org administration) and all `create(org=...)` writes untouched. Smoke-tested all 13 sections as the demo user on the box — **all 200**. The "should see N, see 0" class is gone.

## 2. WidgetCart environment indicator
Hull now injects **`HELM_ENV`** + **`HELM_PROJECT`** into every deployment (both the compose builder and the process runtime), so any app can show its environment. WidgetCart uses it for an unmistakable visual difference:

| | Banner | Accent | Tag |
|---|---|---|---|
| **prod** | 🟢 green "PRODUCTION" | green | `PRODUCTION` |
| **staging** | 🟡 yellow "STAGING" | amber | `STAGING` |

Also reflected in the `<title>`, `/healthz` (`{"env":"prod",...}`), and the log lines (`INFO [prod] heartbeat...`). Re-imported WidgetCart on the box and verified the live public URLs:
- `widgetcart-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com` → 🟢 PRODUCTION
- `widgetcart-staging.apps.dev-reservclaims.com` → 🟡 STAGING

So in the demo you can open both side-by-side and they're visibly different deployments of the same app. Everything's committed, pushed to the public repo, and live on EC2.

## 👤 User

in widgetcart, how do i trigger the error/incident?

### 🤖 Assistant

In WidgetCart, the planted bug is on two routes — **`/boom`** and **`/checkout`** — both return HTTP 500 and log an `ERROR` line. The default monitor fires a SEV2 incident when the error rate exceeds **25% over a 5-minute window**, so you need a burst of 500s (a handful, since the baseline is low traffic).

**Easiest — in the browser:** open the deployment and visit `/checkout` (or `/boom`), then hit refresh ~10–15 times:
- Prod: `https://widgetcart-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com/checkout`
- Staging: `https://widgetcart-staging.apps.dev-reservclaims.com/checkout`

**Cleaner for a demo — fire a burst from your terminal** (type this with the `!` prefix in the session, or any shell):

```
for i in $(seq 1 30); do curl -s -o /dev/null https://widgetcart-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com/boom; done
```

Then watch it land in Hull (give the log tail + monitor a few seconds):
- **Observability** (`/obs/`) → the widgetcart-prod card shows the error spike + red error log lines
- **Incidents** (`/obs/incidents/`) → a new SEV2 **MonitorBreach** incident appears

A few notes for the demo:
- `/checkout` reads better on stage than `/boom` — the 500 page and log line say *"checkout failed: inventory service returned a malformed price."*
- Use the **prod** URL if you want the incident on production; the two environments are independent deployments, so each has its own monitor and incidents.
- It's idempotent — the monitor re-fires occurrences on the same incident rather than spamming new ones, so you can keep hitting it during the talk.

Want me to fire a burst at prod right now so there's a live incident already sitting in the UI for you to walk into?

---

=== HostProxyMiddleware ===
"""Host-based deployment routing.

If an inbound request's Host header matches an ACTIVE custom Domain bound to an
environment, this middleware reverse-proxies the request straight to that
deployment's process/container — BEFORE Hull's session/CSRF/auth/url routing.
That gives every deployment a real hostname (e.g.
``acme-prod.apps.dev-reservclaims.com``) instead of the ``/d/<pk>/`` path.

Control-plane traffic (the Hull dashboard host, localhost, etc.) has no matching
Domain row, so it passes straight through to normal routing. The legacy
``/d/<pk>/`` path proxy stays mounted as a fallback (the autonomous loop uses it).
"""

from __future__ import annotations


class HostProxyMiddleware:
    def __init__(self, get_response):
        self.get_response = get_response

    def __call__(self, request):
        # Lazy import: views pulls in requests/models; keep middleware import light.
        from .views import _proxy_to, _resolve_env_by_host

        try:
            environment = _resolve_env_by_host(request)
        except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — never let routing lookup 500 the site
            environment = None

### 🤖 Assistant

It works now — confirmed end-to-end:

- **30 × HTTP 500** ingested as LogLines (`500s 30, errors 30`)
- Monitor `error_rate > 25%` → **`live_status: alerting`**
- **🚨 INC-2 [SEV2] MonitorBreach** fired and is now `remediating` (the autonomous loop already picked it up)
- The compose tailer is now running **inside gunicorn** (`docker compose -p hull-widgetcart-prod logs -f`), so it persists

## Why it failed before, and the fix
The compose log tailer was only started as a short-lived thread *at deploy time*. When I re-imported WidgetCart via a one-shot script, that thread died on exit — so nothing was ingesting the container's logs. No logs → no error metric → monitor never breached → no incident. (The process runtime already had an "adoption" mechanism for this; compose didn't.)

I added proper adoption:
1. **`ensure_compose_log_tail()`** — idempotently (re)attaches a `docker compose -p <name> logs -f` tee feeding ingestion; tails by project name so it works even without the compose file.
2. **`ensure_tailers()`** is now runtime-aware (compose → tee, process → file tailer).
3. **The host-proxy middleware** calls `ensure_tailers()` whenever someone visits a live app — so just **loading the WidgetCart page (inside the long-lived server) attaches its tailer** before you click the button. The Hull dashboard/feed also trigger it on load.

## For your demo
It's now self-healing, but the reliable sequence is: **open the WidgetCart page first** (that adopts the tailer), then click **🧨 Trigger incident — break checkout**, then switch to Hull's Incidents tab. Within a few seconds the SEV2 MonitorBreach appears.

One heads-up: there's already a live **INC-2** sitting in `remediating` on prod from my test. Want me to resolve/clear it so you start the demo from a clean slate?
